< Review>
(Update) 2 Star Apple Fritter
Good selection but overpriced.  I Considering myself as an apple fritter connoisseur I would rate their fritter a solid C-.  For $1.95, its was on the small side and it used standard glaze, and there was just a hint of apple.  They cooked it like a standard donut, so no crisping on the edges, or those morsel chunks on the fringes.  I have a pretty high standards when it comes to the big boy on the block, and Spudnuts has really lowered their standards but raised the price.  I‚Äôll drive the distance to bypass this shop for a more worthy and less priced A.F.<//Review>

< review>
Pretty cool donut shop. While the inside and outside might be old, the store delivers some good eats and drinks.

They even have a drive thru, or you can go inside to order,  and if you want they also have online ordering too.

They got the regular donuts, buttermilk,  bars, dipped, donut holes, apple fritters and with the crunchy toppings on this as well.  They have breakfast croissant with egg, cheese, bacon sausage and ham too.  If you have raised a cronut(donut made from crossiant) they got these delicious items too.

They have coffee and teas and numerous cans and bottle drinks too. But the funky monkey was awesome.  Start with some espresso,  add icecream and a banana blend it up together,  add some caramel drizzle and top with whip cream and you got your breakfast drink ready togo.

Parking in front and back side makes plenty of spots.< /review>

< text>
This is by far the best donut drive-thru place in the Sacramento Arden area. Apple fritters taste like Apple Hill quality & they make breakfast bagel & croissant sandwiches, with various coffee drinks, smoothies, and Chai or Thai teas available. I've been going here for over 30 years & the people are always amazing & the donuts are home-made & excellent!</text>

< review>
Of all the barber shops I have been to, Temecula Barber Company is one of the very best.  Rene makes you feel welcome the moment you walk in by offering you a warm greeting and a fresh beverage (whiskey, scotch, beer, or water) and then he makes you feel like a valued client by taking a few minutes to talk to you to try to find out exactly what you are going for as far as your hairstyle is concerned before he ever picks the clippers up.  He is a true professional that honors his appointments and offers friendly conversation.  Temecula Barber Company reminds me of the ol' time barber shop where you can go just to step away from life and enjoy getting cleaned up by someone whom takes the craft of barbering seriously.  I will not go to any other barber so long as Rene is in town.  I would give this business 10 stars if I were allowed to.</review>

<user_id>108685370139018629938< /user_id>< name>
Jay Keyes< /name>
< Time>
1556012402796< /Time>
< rating>
3</rating>
< text>
Carl's Jr.'s menu holds very limited appeal to me. For food that is supposedly fast, I never seem to be able to get out of Carl's Jr. with my order in hand in any less than 15 minutes. Their lackluster burgers seemingly take just as long as Five Guys' or In-n-Out's to prepare, yet are significantly inferior in every way. The fries are a lame impression of McDonald's. Aside from the limited run of the "Babyback Rib Burger," I can't think of anything I've ever ordered for lunch or dinner at CJ's that I haven't immediately regretted. The aforementioned rib burger was like an upgraded McRib with crunchy onion straws but alas no longer available.

The breakfast menu at CJ's is somewhat better. I don't hate the "Sausage Egg and Cheese Biscuit." In fact, their biscuit may be the very best biscuit in fast food currently. The egg is a bit weird, like very thinly rendered egg that has the girth and lightness of a folded napkin. Also, like a lot of fast food "yellow egg product," the flavor is more aggressively "eggy" than you'd expect -- and certainly moreso than if you scrambled an egg at home. My solution? Order without the egg. You won't miss it.

This is a co-branded Green Burrito/Carl's Jr. restaurant. There exists approximately 300 of these co-branded Green Burrito/Carl's Jr. stores, almost exclusively in the western and southwestern United States. Despite being located in the middle of University City, this particular location's drive-thru intercom system is ghetto, ensuring you need to repeat your order fourteen times on average before the order-taker understands you. Other than that, I'd consider this to be an "average" Green Burrito/Carl's Jr. location.<//text>
